   // ensures js doesn't die if ads service fails.  
            // Note that we need to define the js here, since ad js is being rendered inline after this.
            (function(f) {
                // Fallback javascript, when the ad Service call fails.  
                
                if((window.csm === undefined || window.generic === undefined || window.consoleLog === undefined)) {
                    if (console !== undefined &amp;&amp; console.log !== undefined) {
                        console.log("one or more of window.csm, window.generic or window.consoleLog has been stubbed...");

               <div class="rec-outline">
                <p>
                 A woman who moves into an apartment across the hall from two brilliant but socially awkward physicists shows them how little they know about life outside of the laboratory.
                </p>
               </div>

       <div class="article" id="titleStoryLine">
        <span class="rightcornerlink">
         <a href="/register/login?why=edit&amp;ref_=tt_stry" rel="login">

         </a>
        </span>
        <h2>
         Storyline
        </h2>
        <div class="inline canwrap" itemprop="description">
         <p>
          In 2012, Louisiana State Police Detectives Rust Cohle and Martin Hart are brought in to revisit a homicide case they worked in 1995. As the inquiry unfolds in present day through separate interrogations, the two former detectives narrate the story of their investigation, reopening unhealed wounds, and drawing into question their supposed solving of a bizarre ritualistic murder in 1995. The timelines braid and converge in 2012 as each man is pulled back into a world they believed they'd left behind. In learning about each other and their killer, it becomes clear that darkness lives on both sides of the law.
          <em class="nobr">
           Written by
           <a href="/search/title?plot_author=Rich28&amp;view=simple&amp;sort=alpha&amp;ref_=tt_stry_pl">
            Rich28
           </a>
          </em>
         </p>
        </div>

        <h2>
         Did You Know?
        </h2>
        <div class="txt-block" id="trivia">
         <h4>
          Trivia
         </h4>
         Creator and writer
         <a href="/name/nm4446305?ref_=tt_trv_trv">
          Nic Pizzolatto
         </a>
         acknowledged the strong influence of Thomas Ligotti's and
         <a href="/name/nm1194127?ref_=tt_trv_trv">
          Emil Cioran
         </a>
         's philosophical writings on the series: "I'd already been reading E.M. Cioran for years and consider him one of my all-time favorite and, oddly, most nourishing writers. As an aphorist, Cioran has no rivals other than perhaps Nietzsche, and many of his philosophies are echoed by Ligotti".[2014]
         <a class="nobr" href="trivia?ref_=tt_trv_trv">
          See more
         </a>
         
        </div>
        <hr/>
        <div class="txt-block" id="goofs">
         <h4>
          Goofs
         </h4>
         Detective Rust Cohle is seen looking at his watch as it beeps. His watch is a mechanical dive watch without any digital components, and is unable to beep.
         <a class="nobr" href="trivia?tab=gf&amp;ref_=tt_trv_gf">
          See more
         </a>
         
        </div>

       <div class="article" id="titleUserReviewsTeaser">
        <h2>
         User Reviews
        </h2>
        <div class="user-comments">
         <div class="tinystarbar" title="10/10">
          <div style="width: 100px;">
          </div>
         </div>
         <span itemprop="review" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
          <strong itemprop="name">
           Amazingly haunting and beautiful
          </strong>
          <span itemprop="reviewRating" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/Rating">
           <meta content="1" itemprop="worstRating"/>
           <meta content="10" itemprop="ratingValue"/>
           <meta content="10" itemprop="bestRating"/>
          </span>
          <div class="comment-meta">
           20 January 2014 | by
           <a href="/user/ur18823361/?ref_=tt_urv">
            <span itemprop="author">
             karen_ga
            </span>
           </a>
           <meta content="2014-01-20" itemprop="datePublished"/>
           (United States)
                        
           <a href="/user/ur18823361/comments?ref_=tt_urv">
            See all my reviews
           </a>
          </div>
          <div>
           <p itemprop="reviewBody">
            Of course, I knew that HBO was putting this out there. What I didn't expect was to be hooked from the opening titles. Atmospheric, moody, moving at the laconic pace of South (not to be confused with slow). We, as viewers, are watching the story unfold just as the characters do. Harrelson and McConaughey are simply and elegantly perfect, playing off of each other to the perfect degree. The cinematography is stellar, as is the story as it begins to unfold. I had no idea what I was in for when I turned it on, but I'm hooked, and can't wait for the next and the next and the next...secrets abound, tantalizing clues are everywhere, but where do they lead. I'm can't wait to find out.
           </p>
          </div>
         </span>
         <hr/>
